107 (933)
Daksin╠г ╠гa╠Д (Priestly Gift) or Its Givers
Divya ─Ас╣Еgirasa or Dakс╣гiс╣З─Б Pr─Бj─Бpaty─Б
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 4
These extravagant praises of the dakс╣гiс╣З─Б (тАЬpriestly giftтАЭ), which is given by the sacrificer to the various priests who officiate at his sacrifice, are clearly in the poetтАЩs interests, as he stands to receive a portion of the sacrificerтАЩs largesse. The hymn sel dom strays from its pointтАФthat a dakс╣гiс╣З─Б, once given, brings untold benefits to the giver, both material and spiritual, far exceeding the value of the original gift. It is a persuasive, if somewhat monotone, piece of work.

English translation:

тАЬThe great (splendour) of Maghavan has becomemanifest (for the rites) of these (worshippers); all lifehas been extricated from darkness, the vast light bestowed by the progenitors has arrived, a spacious path forthe dakс╣гiс╣З─Б has been displayed. (I Maghavan: Mqaghavan = the sun, at whose rising and at midday thedakс╣гiс╣З─Б is to be given, not at sunset; cf. RV. 5.77.2].тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Their great generosity has been revealed. All life has been freed from darkness;
the great light, given by the forefathers, has come. The wide path for the priestly gift has become visible.

Griffith

THESE men’s great bounty hath been manifested, and the whole world of life set free from darkness.
Great light hath come, vouchsafed us by the Fathers: apparent is the spacious path of Guerdon.

Geldner

Jetzt hat sich deren gro├Яe Freigebigkeit geoffenbart; alles Lebende ist jetzt von der Finsternis erl├╢st. Das gro├Яe, von den V├дtern gespendete Licht ist gekommen: Der breite Weg der Daksina ist sichtbar geworden.

Grassmann

Es hat sich offenbart die grosse Freigiebigkeit dieser M├дnner, alles Lebende hat sich der Dunkelheit entwunden; das von den V├дtern verliehene grosse Licht ist gekommen, der breite Weg des Opferlohnes hat sich gezeigt.

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдз рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рджрд┐ рд╢реБрднрдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рджреЗрдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ, рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░ рдореЗрдВ рдпрд╢рд╕реНрдХрд░реА рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рддреНрдо рд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рдж рд╣реИ, рдкрд░ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛рджрд╛рддрд╛ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдп рдмрдирддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рд╣реИрдВред

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рджрд┐рд╢реБрднрдХрд░реНрдорд╕реБ рджрд╛рддрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░реЗ рдпрд╢рд╕реНрдХрд░реА рддрдерд╛рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рддреНрдорд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рджрд╛рддрд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛рджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдГ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдордирдГ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпреЗрд╡рдорд╛рджрдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ред

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Saram─Б). I come, the appointed messenger of Indra, desiring, Paс╣Зis, your great hidden treasures;through fear of being crossed the (water) helped us, thus I passed over the waters of the Ras─Б.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

High above in heaven have they taken their standтАФthose providing the priestly gift. Those who give horses, they (come) together with the sun; those giving gold receive a share in immortality; those giving garments extend their own lifetime, o Soma.

Griffith

High up in heaven abide the Guerdon-givers: they who give steeds dwell with the Sun for ever.
They who give gold are blest with life eternal. they who give robes prolong their lives, O Soma.

Geldner

Hoch oben im Himmel haben die Daksinageber ihren Stand, die Rosseschenker, die sind bei der Sonne. Die Goldschenker werden der Unsterblichkeit teilhaft, die Kleidschenker verl├дngern ihr Leben, o Soma.

Grassmann

Hoch zum Himmel haben sich die Geber des Opferlohnes erhoben; die Geber der Rosse sind mit der Sonne vereint; die Geber des Goldes erlangen Unsterblichkeit; die Geber von Kleidern, o Soma, verl├дngern ihr Leben.

Elizarenkova

Jamison Brereton

The priestly gift is the divine bestowal, a sacrificial offering to the gods; it is not for the stingy, for they do not bestow.
But many men who present priestly gifts bestow through fear of disgrace.

Griffith

Not from the niggards-for they give not fireely-comes Meed at sacrifice, Gods’ satisfaction:
Yea, many men with hands stretched out with Guerdon present their gifts because they dread dishonour.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Saram─Б). I do not believe that he can be subdued; he as whose messenger I have come to thisplace from afar subdues (his enemies). The deep rivers do not conceal him; you, Paс╣Зis, slain by Indra, will sleep(in death).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Those with manly sight see (it as) the wind with its hundred streams (of rain), (as) the chant that finds the sun; they see (it as) the oblation.
Those who bestow and present at the (sacrificial) assembly, they milk the priestly gift with its seven mothers.

Griffith

These who observe mankind regard oblation as streamy Vayu and light-finding Arka.
They satisfy and give their gifts in synod, and pour in streams the seven-mothered Guerdon.

Geldner

Sie sehen darin den Wind, der hundert Regeng├╝sse bringt, den Lobgesang, der die Sonne auffindet; mit Kenneraugen sehen diese ein Opfer darin. Die welche in der Opferversammlung schenken und spenden, die melken die Daksina, die sieben M├╝tter hat.

Grassmann

Den hundertstr├╢migen V─Бju, die Licht bringende Sonne und des M├дnnerbeschauers [Agni] Opfertrank haben diejenigen im Auge, welche reichlich schenken und Gaben darreichen bei der Opferversammlung, sie melken aus die Opferkuh mit sieben K├дlbern.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Saram─Б). Your words, Paс╣Зis, are not in the plural ce of armies; your sinful bodies will not be equal toarrows. Let your path be difficult to follow, let Bс╣Ыhaspati show no favour to either (your words or your person ns).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Armies: aseny─Б = sen─Бrh─Бс╣Зi na bhavanti, your words are not equal to armies, i.e., your words are not to befeared;

Aniс╣гavyaс╕е = i┼Ыvarh─Бс╣Зi na santu par─Бkramar─Бhityena, let them not be equal to arrows through yourabsence of prowess

Jamison Brereton

They say that just he is the seer, he the creator of sacred formulations, the leader of the sacrifice, the singer of chants, the reciter of
solemn words.
He knows the three bodies of the blazing oneтАФhe who first found
success with the priestly gift.

Griffith

They call him Rsi, Brahman, Sama-chanter, reciter of the laud, leader of worship.
The brightly-shining God’s three forms he knoweth who first bestowed the sacrificial Guerdon.

Geldner

Den nennen sie den eigentlichen Rishi, den den Brahman, den Opferleiter, den Samas├дnger, den Liedvortrager, der kennt die drei K├╢rper des Lichts, der zuerst die Daksina zugef├╝hrt hat.

Grassmann

Den wahrlich nennt man einen Dichter, den einen Brahmanen, einen Leiter des Opfers, einen Lieds├дnger, einen Spruchsager, der kennt die drei Gestalten des gl├дnzenden [Agni], welcher zuerst mit dem Opferlohn zu Stande gekommen ist.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬ(The Paс╣Зis). This treasure, Saram─Б, secured in the mountain is composed of cows, horses andriches; the Paс╣Зis protect it who are good watchers; you have come to this lonely spot in vain.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Lonely =resounding with the lowing of the oxen

Jamison Brereton

The priestly gift gives the horse; the priestly gift the cow; the priestly gift the lustrous and what is golden.
The priestly gift wins the food that is our very lifebreath. He who
understands makes the priestly gift his armor.

Griffith

Guerdon bestows the horse, bestows the bullock, Guerdon bestows, moreover, gold that Rsisters.
Guerdon gives food which is our life and spirit. He who is wise takes Guerdon for his armour.

Geldner

Die Daksina schenkt das Ro├Я, die Daksina ein Rind, die Daksina Gold und Silber. Die Daksina bringt Speise ein, die unser Lebenshauch ist, die Daksina macht der Wissende zu seinem Panzer.

Grassmann

Der Opferlohn gibt das Ross, der Opferlohn das Rind, der Opferlohn auch das gl├дnzende Gold; der Opferlohn verschafft Speise; er ist unser Lebenshauch; wer klug ist, macht sich den Opferlohn zu seinem Panzer.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Saram─Б). Excited by the Soma, the с╣Ъс╣гis, the Aс╣Еgirasas of the nine months’ rite, headed by Ayasya,will come here; they will partition this herd of cattle, then the Paс╣Зis will retract their words.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Headed by Ayasya:or, unwearying; will retract their words: liс╣н, vomit, i.e., reject

Jamison Brereton

The benefactors have not died, nor have they gone to a failed end; the benefactors are not harmed, nor do they falter.
What is this whole world and the sun, all this does the priestly gift give to them.

Griffith

The liberal die not, never are they ruined: the liberal suffer neither harm nor trouble.
The light of heaven, the universe about us,-all this doth sacrificial Guerdon give them.

Geldner

Die Gastfreien sterben nicht, sie haben nie einen Fehlgang getan; die Gastfreien nehmen keinen Schaden, sie kommen nie zu Fall. Diese ganze Welt und das Himmelslicht, das alles gibt ihnen die Daksina.

Grassmann

Die Freigiebigen sterben nicht, sie gerathen nicht ins Elend; die Freigiebigen leiden nicht Schaden, sie wanken nimmer; was diese ganze Welt, was das Lichtreich in sich fasst, das alles gibt der Opferlohn den Gebern.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(The Paс╣Зis). You have indeed come here, Saram─Б, constrained by divine power; we will make youour sister, do not return, we will share the cattle with you auspicious one.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The benefactors at first won the sweet-smelling womb; the benefactors won a bride who is richly dressed.
The benefactors won the right to the inner drinking of liquor. The
benefactors won (against those) who come forward uninvited.

Griffith

First have the liberal gained a fragrant dwelling, and got themselves a bride in fair apparel.
The liberal have obtained their draught of liquor, and conquered those who, unprovoked, assailed them.

Geldner

Die Gastfreien haben zuerst den duftigen Frauenscho├Я errungen, die Gastfreien haben die Braut errungen, die sch├╢ngekleidet ist. Die Gastfreien haben das Recht auf das Einschl├╝rfen des Branntweins errungen; die Gastfreien tragen den Sieg davon ├╝ber die, welche ungebeten erscheinen.

Grassmann

Den Freigiebigen gewinnen zuerst den sch├╢numfangenden Schoos [Wohnsitz], die Freigiebigen gewinnen die sch├╢ngekleidete Gattin, die Freigiebigen erlangen das Einschl├╝rfen des Sur─Б-trankes; die Freigiebigen ├╝berholen die, welche uneingeladen vor ihnen hergehen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬ(Saram─Б). I recognize not fraternity nor sisterhood; Indra and the terrible Aс╣Еgirasas know (mykindred); my (masters) desiring the cattle overshadowed (yoru habitation) when I came; depart hence, Paс╣Зis to adistant (spot).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For the benefactor they groom the swift horse; for the benefactor the maiden sits waiting, making herself beautiful.
This dwelling of the benefactor is like a lotus-pond, adorned and
shimmering like the palaces of the gods.

Griffith

They deck the fleet steed for the bounteous giver: the maid adorns herself and waits to meet him.
His home is like a lake with lotus blossoms, like the Gods’ palaces adorned and splendid.

рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрд╡рд╛рд╣рдГ рее тАШ рд╡рд╣ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдгреЗ ’ ред тАЬ рд╡рд╣рд╢реНрдЪ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдгреНрд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рд╢реЛрднрдирд╡рд╣рдирд╕рдорд░реНрдерд╛рдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рднреЛрдЬрдВ рджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╡рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдВ рджреЗрд╢рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рддрддрдГ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рджрд╛рддреБрд░реНрдпрдВрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╕реБрд╡реГрддреН рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдЪрдХреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рд╡рд░реНрддрдирдВ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕реЛрд╜рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рд╕рд╣рд┐рддрдГ рд░рдердГ рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдЕрде рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдГ ред рд╣реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ рд╣реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рджрдпрдГ рднрд░реЗрд╖реБ ред рднреНрд░рд┐рдпрдд’ рдЖрд╣рд╡рдиреАрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд░реВрдкреЗрдгрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рддреНрд░реЗрддрд┐ рднрд░рд╛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред тАШ рднреД рднрд░реНрддреНрд╕рдиреЗ ’ ред рднреГрдгрдиреНрддрд┐ рднрд░реНрддреНрд╕рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдпреЛрджреНрдзрд╛рд░ рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрддрд┐ рднрд░рд╛рдГ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдорд╛рдГ ред рддреЗрд╖реБ рднреЛрдЬрдВ рджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдореН рдЕрд╡рдд рд░рдХреНрд╖рдд ред рддрддреЛ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдкрд╛рд▓рд┐рддрдГ рднреЛрдЬрдГ рдзрдирд╛рджрд┐рджрд╛рдиреЗрди рдЬрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рднреЛрдЬрдпрд┐рддрд╛ рд╕рдиреН рд╕рдордиреАрдХреЗрд╖реБ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЬреЗрддрд╛ рдЬрдпрд╢реАрд▓реЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред тАШ рдЬрд┐ рдЬрдпреЗ’ред рддрд╛рдЪреНрдЫреАрд▓рд┐рдХрд╕реНрддреГрдиреН ред рдЕрдд рдПрд╡ тАШ рди рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рд╡реНрдпрдп┬░ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрдп рд╖рд╖реНрдареАрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ ред рее рек рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGo hence, Paс╣Зis, to a far-off distant (spot), let the cattle come forth in due order bursting through (thedoor) the concealed cattle which Bс╣Ыhaspati, the Soma, the grinding stones and the wise с╣Ъс╣гis have found.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The steadily conveying horses convey the benefactor. Rolling easily, the chariot of the priestly gift rolls on.
O gods, help the benefactor in the raids. The benefactor will win against his rivals at the encounters (with them).

Griffith

Steeds good at draught convey the liberal giver, and lightly rolling moves the car of Guerdon.
Assist, ye Gods, the liberal man in battles: the liberal giver conquers foes in combat.

Geldner

Den Gastfreien ziehen gutziehende Rosse, leicht rollt der Wagen der Daksina. O G├╢tter, beg├╝nstiget den Gastfreien in den Preisk├дmpfen! Der Gastfreie wird in den Schlachten Sieger ├╝ber die Feinde sein!

Grassmann

Die Freigiebigen fahren trefflich fahrende Rosse, leicht rollt der Wagen des Opferlohners; den Freigiebigen unterst├╝tzt, o ihr G├╢tter, in den K├дmpfen; der Freigiebige besiegt die Feinde in den Schlachten.

Elizarenkova

  • рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпреЛ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдкрддреНрдпрд╛
  • рдирд┐рдЪреГрддреНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН
  • рдзреИрд╡рддрдГ
рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рднреЛрдЬрдореН) рдкрд╛рд▓рдХ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рдХреЛ(рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрд╡рд╛рд╣рдГ) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рд▓реЗ рдЬрд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рдШреЛреЬреЗ (рд╡рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐)рд▓реЗ рдЬрд╛рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ (рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ) рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкреА рдХрд╛рд░реАрдЧрд░рдХреЛ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреА рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛ рджреЗрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдШреВрдордиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд░рде рдорд┐рд▓рддрд╛ рд╣реИ (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ) рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдп рдХреЗ рдЗрдЪреНрдЫреБрдХ рд╕реИрдирд┐рдХреЛ ! (рднрд░реЗрд╖реБ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рднреЛрдЬрдореН) рдкрд╛рд▓рдХ рдХреА (рдЕрд╡рдд) рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░реЛ (рднреЛрдЬрдГ) рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рд╕рдордиреАрдХреЗрд╖реБ)рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░ рд╕рдореНрдореБрдЦ рдпреЛрджреНрдзрд╛рдУрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЬреЗрддрд╛) рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬреАрддреЗрдЧрд╛, рдРрд╕рд╛ рд╢реАрд▓рд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерезрезрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛрд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рдирдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЙрд╕реЗ рдШреЛреЬреЗ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреА рд╕рд╡рд╛рд░реА рджреЗрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВред рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреА рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛ рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рджреЗрдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ, рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдпрд╛рди рдмрдирд╛рдПрдБред рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╕реИрдирд┐рдХ рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреА рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╣реА рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░ рд▓реЬрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬреАрддрдиреЗ рдХрд╛ рд╢реАрд▓ рд░рдЦрддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерезрезрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рднреЛрдЬрдВ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрд╡рд╛рд╣рдГ-рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╡рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐) рднреЛрдЬрдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирдВ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрд╡рд╛рд╣рдХрд╛ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрдиреБрдХреВрд▓рдВ рдирдпрдиреНрддрд┐ (рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ-рд╕реБрд╡реГрддреН-рд░рдердГ-рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ) рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкрд┐рдиреЗ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛рджрд╛рдирд╛рддреН рдЦрд▓реБ рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрддрдиреЛ рд░рдердГ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗред рдЕрде рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдХреГрддрдореБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ) рд╣реЗ рдЬрд┐рдЧрдорд┐рд╖рд╡реЛ рдпреВрдпрдВ (рднрд░реЗрд╖реБ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ (рднреЛрдЬрдореН) рдкрд╛рд▓рдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрдВ (рдЕрд╡рдд) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдд (рднреЛрдЬрдГ) рднреЛрдЬрдпрд┐рддрд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрдГ (рд╕рдордиреАрдХреЗрд╖реБ) рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рд╕рдореНрдореБрдЦрднреВрддреЗрд╖реБ рдпреЛрджреНрдзреГрд╖реБ (рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЬреЗрддрд╛) рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЬреЗрд╖реНрдпрддреАрддрд┐ рддрдЪреНрдЫреАрд▓реЛ рднреЛрдЬ рдПрд╡ реерезрезрее
